  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer14185630162669910244">Jace Mongomery was a stranger in Chandler. Tall, proud, and ruggedly handsome, he would make any woman's heart beat faster...<br/><br/>Even shy, sweet Nellie Grayson -- Nellie, who thought only of her beautiful younger sister's happiness.   <span id="freeText14185630162669910244" style="display:none">Jace Mongomery was a stranger in Chandler. Tall, proud, and ruggedly handsome, he would make any woman's heart beat faster...<br /><br />Even shy, sweet Nellie Grayson -- Nellie, who thought only of her beautiful younger sister's happiness. With Nellie's tireless aid, Terel Grayson easily became the belle of Chandler, Colorado.<br /><br />Yet Jace, homesick for his closeknit family in Maine, took immediately to Nellie. For the first time, Nellie was the center of attention. It was a heady, delightful feeling...almost as wonderful as the moment when Jace gave her her very first kiss.<br /><br />Nellie was sure her romantic idyll would end -- how long could Jace resist the lovely Terel's charms? But with the help of an enchanting new friend, Nellie would discover that her flirtatious sister might not be the woman to win the gallant Jace Montgomery....</span>

<div id="review_321327751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321327751" />
    <a title="S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9160774-s"><img alt="S" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321327751?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S" href="/user/show/9160774-s">S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780743459433" href="/book/show/7308849-wishes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321327751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14509031770099322343">he Heroine (and that's stretching it a bit) is one of the most pathetic characters I've about in awhile. She spends more than half the book as a doormat with perhaps two little acts of defiance. TWO! And the romance between Nellie and her love is cute but not sizzling. Personally I thought the most interesting character in the book was perhaps Berni and that was even stretching it abit. I spent most of my time not focusing on the romance but on Nellies complete and utter nativity and total lack </span>
  <span id="freeText14509031770099322343" style="display:none">he Heroine (and that's stretching it a bit) is one of the most pathetic characters I've about in awhile. She spends more than half the book as a doormat with perhaps two little acts of defiance. TWO! And the romance between Nellie and her love is cute but not sizzling. Personally I thought the most interesting character in the book was perhaps Berni and that was even stretching it abit. I spent most of my time not focusing on the romance but on Nellies complete and utter nativity and total lack of self esteem. I wanted desperately for her to see her own worth and stand up for herself instead of Jace always giving her a pep talk. How can you even begin to love someone else if you don't even love yourself first or at the very least have a little self respect? <br /><br />Now for her sister Terel. If you really want to picture Terel just think of that mean popular chick in high school who has the face of angel but always gives back handed compliments like "You know what you'd be really pretty if it weren't that zit on your nose" Yeah remember her? She's here and poor Nellie of course always stuffs her face with every criticism her sister doles out. So yes please save your money and yourself a little aggravation and pass on this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14509031770099322343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313988399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14938251655650294774">WARNING: This is NOT a better love story than Twilight. And that's about as harsh as one can get.<br/><br/>Definitely one of the weirdest books I've ever read. At the end of it all, I don't get what the book was trying to say. That true love triumphs over every obstacle? Scratch that, magic trumps it all. Why introduce any conflict at all if you would fix them with a Deux (or Douche) Machina fairy godmother? If the fairy godmother could've made people fall in love with whomever, why did we even have this </span>
  <span id="freeText14938251655650294774" style="display:none">WARNING: This is NOT a better love story than Twilight. And that's about as harsh as one can get.<br /><br />Definitely one of the weirdest books I've ever read. At the end of it all, I don't get what the book was trying to say. That true love triumphs over every obstacle? Scratch that, magic trumps it all. Why introduce any conflict at all if you would fix them with a Deux (or Douche) Machina fairy godmother? If the fairy godmother could've made people fall in love with whomever, why did we even have this book?<br />That you reap what you sow? Hah! There is no such thing as comeuppance. Apparently, selfishness and cruelty will get you exactly where kindness and self-sacrifice will, but with much less effort.<br />That despite being called fat or overweight, people will still appreciate you as long as you're kind and good? No such thing, let's make the heroine instantly thinner by magic!<br />That the hero liked the overweight heroine because of her golden heart and glowing soul? Nope, he liked her because he had some Oedipus complex going on, as his opera singer mother and her amigas were also overweight. <br /><br />Gaah, this book makes me so angry for being so stupid and pointless. Such a waste of my life. Don't let it waste yours.</span>

        <a title="Tiera McMillian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiera McMillian" href="/user/show/21366500-tiera-mcmillian">Tiera McMillian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer643040223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6328963427878456114">*Reread Review*<br/>This is probably one of my favorite Jude Deveraux books ever! The guardian angel concept, working of sins in purgatory by helping others we teach ourselves life's greatest lessons! This author is a dang genius that's all there is too it! This book has a whole different feel than her other books because Jude writes about strong, fierce women who don't take no for an answer and could rule the world on their worst days.. usually. This FMC though, she is strong in a completely differe</span>
  <span id="freeText6328963427878456114" style="display:none">*Reread Review*<br />This is probably one of my favorite Jude Deveraux books ever! The guardian angel concept, working of sins in purgatory by helping others we teach ourselves life's greatest lessons! This author is a dang genius that's all there is too it! This book has a whole different feel than her other books because Jude writes about strong, fierce women who don't take no for an answer and could rule the world on their worst days.. usually. This FMC though, she is strong in a completely different way and seems ordinary in comparison to the other women but it makes the book all the more touching when she comes into her own. What I love even more is that the blurb doesn't even prepare you for the "fantasy" involved in this romance.<br /><br />Berni our sideline FMC has lived her life only for herself and material objects! Upon her death noone cares they are happy to see her go, to take her place in the social circle. Berni on the other hand ends up in a white waiting room.. it seems she didn't quite earn her keep on earth.. no she must work her way through levels of purgatory if she wants the prize. Her current client Nellie Grayson.. whew what a project. Nellie only lives for others, and has no time for own happy ending, even if come in a deliriously handsome, kind, gentle and wonderful Mongomery male package. Berni thinks Nellie's case is open/shut just give her some wishes to use to make herself happy and make her loose some weight and shell be right as rain... Not everyone uses their wishes for themselves though and as Nellie uses her wishes for her family she becomes a slave to her wishes.. Now Berni has to come in a do some dirty work, and in the process learns that none of those "things" are important and little acts of kindness can change the world slowly but surely.<br /><br />The best thing about this book is that it was set up at the end to continue the story if the author had wanted to. She could have made a whole series about Berni and her clients as she works her way through the levels of Purgatory. Thats still an option.. even thought its been a million years since this book came out.. I still hold out hope. Until then I guess Berni is stuck on level 2.. and those options were horrendous lol.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6328963427878456114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_482922181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482922181" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15692211-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356176146p2/15692211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/482922181?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/15692211-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15692211-rebecca?shelf=historical-and-hot">historical-and-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15692211-rebecca?shelf=bbw-plus-size-woman-hero">bbw-plus-size-woman-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482922181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11681183270369364175">The heroine for the most part is very lovable and beautiful, but I was very annoyed by many things. Her eating out of sadness was realistic and she needed emotional help for it, but since when is 160 pounds considered morbidly obese? If she was 260 I would be concerned. <br/><br/>The hero loved the young lady exactly as she was, so why have her lose weight? It was as though the author wanted everyone to "accept" the girl, and the only way to accomplish this is to make her thin, the way all women "have" to</span>
  <span id="freeText11681183270369364175" style="display:none">The heroine for the most part is very lovable and beautiful, but I was very annoyed by many things. Her eating out of sadness was realistic and she needed emotional help for it, but since when is 160 pounds considered morbidly obese? If she was 260 I would be concerned. <br /><br />The hero loved the young lady exactly as she was, so why have her lose weight? It was as though the author wanted everyone to "accept" the girl, and the only way to accomplish this is to make her thin, the way all women "have" to be.<br /><br />The younger sister is a bitch. We all know that. No need to say more.<br /><br />The modern woman is a bitch too, and ends up learning a good lesson. But the overall effect left me annoyed more than happy.<br /><br />Deveraux is a great and well known writer of womens' romance and is a nice storyteller, but when you sense a refusal or reluctance to create a truly strong character because of society's prescriptions of what women are supposed to be, it takes away from your enjoyment of the story. I loved the heroine and hero anyway, especially the hero. Very rare to find a man falling in love with plus sized woman.<br /><br />This book is one of many that make me prefer gay m/m fiction to m/f fiction! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11681183270369364175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2546175142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16188931231614006715">A delightfully entertaining vision of what it might be like when we die. I was a bit startled to find Berni, having died in the 21st century, being sent back to the 18th to help Nellie. Jace Montgomery is visiting in Colorado with newfound family in the Kane Taggerts when he meets the plump Nellie whose thinner and younger sister has always ruled the roost. Jace doesn't even look at Terel. All he can see is Nellie. Nellie eats so much that I almost felt ill reading about it. For once, I think a </span>
  <span id="freeText16188931231614006715" style="display:none">A delightfully entertaining vision of what it might be like when we die. I was a bit startled to find Berni, having died in the 21st century, being sent back to the 18th to help Nellie. Jace Montgomery is visiting in Colorado with newfound family in the Kane Taggerts when he meets the plump Nellie whose thinner and younger sister has always ruled the roost. Jace doesn't even look at Terel. All he can see is Nellie. Nellie eats so much that I almost felt ill reading about it. For once, I think a book with so much food has put me off the thought of eating. It may be the best diet book I've ever read. It certainly takes your appetite away. If I lose weight over the next few days, I may re-read it sooner rather than later. I loved the ending as well as the beginning, which isn't always a given with Deveraux.</span>

<div id="review_3086253490" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3086253490" />
    <a title="Sanrizz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11233891-sanrizz"><img alt="Sanrizz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600672287p2/11233891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3086253490?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sanrizz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sanrizz" href="/user/show/11233891-sanrizz">Sanrizz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11233891-sanrizz?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11233891-sanrizz?shelf=not-my-favorite">not-my-favorite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3086253490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10899066084276997767"><b>WISHES</b> by Jude Deveraux is about two sisters Nellie and Terel Grayson, and their father, Charles Grayson. Their mother died when Nellie was twelve and Terel four (I think), so since that age, Nellie has assumed the mother role for Terel and is the default maid/cook (slave, actually). <br/><br/><b>
  <u>NOTE TO THE AUTHOR</u>
</b>: I read the Dutch version of the book (my native language) and there are A LOT of incorrect translations and typos in there. Please check that out. You're welcome. <3<br/><br/>The first time I read the </span>
  <span id="freeText10899066084276997767" style="display:none"><b>WISHES</b> by Jude Deveraux is about two sisters Nellie and Terel Grayson, and their father, Charles Grayson. Their mother died when Nellie was twelve and Terel four (I think), so since that age, Nellie has assumed the mother role for Terel and is the default maid/cook (slave, actually). <br /><br /><b>
  <u>NOTE TO THE AUTHOR</u>
</b>: I read the Dutch version of the book (my native language) and there are A LOT of incorrect translations and typos in there. Please check that out. You're welcome. &lt;3<br /><br />The first time I read the book was over ten years ago, <i>I LOVED IT!</i>! So, why not read it again? <br /><br />When I read it for a second time I did not like it as much as the first time. The heroine, Nellie, is so weak, she has absolutely no backbone. I don't know who I wanted to slap first and hardest: Nellie or Terel. <br /><br />I don't like the whole <i>martyr-I-need-to-be-saved-and-told-I-am-beautiful</i> type of heroine. I think there was little to no character development when it came to any of the characters. <br /><br />The fact that the author thought Nellie had to be thinner for her life to improve... that bothered me. And of course, Jace had to be a millionaire...<br /><br />LOL! I don't know, it is a quick read, it is sometimes entertaining, but it wasn't my favorite book. I would not read it again, but I would recommend it to someone who likes to read and doesn't care what they read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10899066084276997767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1627288309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1627288309" />
    <a title="SmartBitches" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43581981-smartbitches"><img alt="SmartBitches" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433165603p2/43581981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1627288309?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SmartBitches" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SmartBitches" href="/user/show/43581981-smartbitches">SmartBitches</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43581981-smartbitches?shelf=a-grade">a-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43581981-smartbitches?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43581981-smartbitches?shelf=historical-not-in-a-ballroom">historical-not-in-a-ballroom</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627288309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8970184110469998769"><b>Full review at <a href='http://smartbitchestrashybooks.com/reviews/wishes-jude-deveraux/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Smart Bitches, Trashy Books</a></b><br/><br/>THIS BOOK WAS COMPLETELY RIDICULOUS.<br/><br/>(I was promised ridiculous and then I got it.)<br/><br/>The core romance is pretty simple – guy meets girl, girl can’t understand why guy is interested, girl’s family conspires to keep girl from leaving them to their own devices. What Devereux does here is give you a book that sets you up for frustration and then gives you satisfaction. When you’re going, “OH MY GOD, YOU FUCKING IDIOTS, WOULD YOU JUST DO A THING,” there’s a char</span>
  <span id="freeText8970184110469998769" style="display:none"><b>Full review at <a href="http://smartbitchestrashybooks.com/reviews/wishes-jude-deveraux/" rel="nofollow noopener">Smart Bitches, Trashy Books</a></b><br /><br />THIS BOOK WAS COMPLETELY RIDICULOUS.<br /><br />(I was promised ridiculous and then I got it.)<br /><br />The core romance is pretty simple – guy meets girl, girl can’t understand why guy is interested, girl’s family conspires to keep girl from leaving them to their own devices. What Devereux does here is give you a book that sets you up for frustration and then gives you satisfaction. When you’re going, “OH MY GOD, YOU FUCKING IDIOTS, WOULD YOU JUST DO A THING,” there’s a character (Berni) who is A, making the same mistake and B, also in a position to do something about it.<br /><br />I really appreciated the commentary on weight – yes, through the power of magic, Nellie suddenly becomes skinny, but NONE of her problems are solved (and none of her clothes fit, which is another expensive problem to fix). Her problems weren’t caused by her weight; her weight was caused by her problems which are primarily the toxic, terrible people around her (and until Berni learns how to person, she’s one of those toxic people).<br /><br />It’s annoying that we can’t have a heroine who is plus-sized and remains so (still a rare unicorn, almost never seen in the wild) but Devereux does make it plain that, “Well, you’d just be fine if you lost weight” isn’t an answer.<br /><br />If it isn’t clear by now, this is a Cinderella story where the fairy godmother has actual learning and growing to do, too. That part was fun, and very silly, and the Cinderella motif was ladled on heavily. There was a ruined gown that gets replaced by a truly pimped-out dress. There was a magic wand. There was comeuppance for Nellie’s stupid family. It was emotionally satisfying, if not terribly complex, and I enjoyed it immensely.<br /><br />- Redheadedgirl</span>
  <a data-text-id="8970184110469998769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kamy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7115442-kamy"><img alt="Kamy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350556866p2/7115442.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer2095364358570589707">This is undoubtedly one of the weirdest books I have ever read. The plot is so unbelievably formulaic, the characters so steroetypically bland that I literally had to suspend any feeling realism in order to get any enjoyment out of this book. Meet Nellie, the most insecure woman on the planet. She could also give the Sugar Plum Fairy a few lessons in niceness and sacrifice. She was ridiculously depressing.<br/><br/>Meet her sister Terel, a selfish, egoistic brat who seriously had not the capacity to consi</span>
  <span id="freeText2095364358570589707" style="display:none">This is undoubtedly one of the weirdest books I have ever read. The plot is so unbelievably formulaic, the characters so steroetypically bland that I literally had to suspend any feeling realism in order to get any enjoyment out of this book. Meet Nellie, the most insecure woman on the planet. She could also give the Sugar Plum Fairy a few lessons in niceness and sacrifice. She was ridiculously depressing.<br /><br />Meet her sister Terel, a selfish, egoistic brat who seriously had not the capacity to consider anyone's well being besides hers. She was ridiculously evil<br /><br />The meet Jace, the only one in the entire book who seemed to show a modicum of sense, though how he put up with the bundle of joy that is Nellie I do not even. <br /><br />Throw in magic, a fairy godmother, a bunch of children and one of the weirdest punishments ever, like seriously I can't even.<br /><br />2 stars, because the dreamer cinderella-lover in me did manage to get some enjoyement out of this, for reasons I would rather not examine.</span>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1187063645" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15015047773826734328">I have mixed feelings about this book. On one hand i obviously enjoyed reading it (finished it one day), but the ending infuriates me. Wishes is another Cinderella story, however, instead of a wicked stepmom and stepsister, we have a cruel father who plays favorites plus an envious and manipulative younger sister. Cinderella, aka Nellie, is kind and beautiful but is an emotional eater so she's overweight. Prince Charming, aka Jace, is a handsome and wealthy widower. And Berni, the fairy godmothe</span>
  <span id="freeText15015047773826734328" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this book. On one hand i obviously enjoyed reading it (finished it one day), but the ending infuriates me. Wishes is another Cinderella story, however, instead of a wicked stepmom and stepsister, we have a cruel father who plays favorites plus an envious and manipulative younger sister. Cinderella, aka Nellie, is kind and beautiful but is an emotional eater so she's overweight. Prince Charming, aka Jace, is a handsome and wealthy widower. And Berni, the fairy godmother, is a dead person trying to atone for her misdemeanors. I like the authors' idea of the afterlife, I like Jace and Berni, but I dislike it that Nellie's character remained weak. I wanted her to stand up to her abusive father and sister and for them to at least show remorse for everything they put her through. She deserved a better "happily ever after."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1780225366650959452">This is my favorite romance novel of all time. I first read it in high school (which may be one reason I hold it so dear) but I've just adored it ever since. It is a fantasy romance, a fairy tale, really. It is more fantasy-based than Deveraux's other novels. I've read some negative reviews, and I suppose that if one doesn't approach the novel as being a fairy tale (there is a fairy godmother!) then one might be disappointed. But as long as you are expecting a fairy tale and are willing to suspe</span>
  <span id="freeText1780225366650959452" style="display:none">This is my favorite romance novel of all time. I first read it in high school (which may be one reason I hold it so dear) but I've just adored it ever since. It is a fantasy romance, a fairy tale, really. It is more fantasy-based than Deveraux's other novels. I've read some negative reviews, and I suppose that if one doesn't approach the novel as being a fairy tale (there is a fairy godmother!) then one might be disappointed. But as long as you are expecting a fairy tale and are willing to suspend a bit of disbelief, then this book is just freaking fabulous. So fun. So, so, so fun. Really, I can't say much more.<br /></span>

I re-read it from time to time to remind myself that true beauty lies within. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134591790" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4167262-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383922141p2/4167262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2134591790?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/4167262-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2134591790&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134591790" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15604696867622471617">I honestly don't know how I feel about this book. It was like watching a train wreck; I wanted to stop reading but I just couldn't look away. I feel like there was supposed to be a lesson in there somewhere, but I have no idea what it was.<br/>I was filled with rage about Berni being sent to "The Kitchen" after death and thought there was going to be some inside joke, and that the author was making a statement about women's rights or something, but NOPE. There's really no reason why Limbo is called t</span>
  <span id="freeText15604696867622471617" style="display:none">I honestly don't know how I feel about this book. It was like watching a train wreck; I wanted to stop reading but I just couldn't look away. I feel like there was supposed to be a lesson in there somewhere, but I have no idea what it was.<br />I was filled with rage about Berni being sent to "The Kitchen" after death and thought there was going to be some inside joke, and that the author was making a statement about women's rights or something, but NOPE. There's really no reason why Limbo is called the Kitchen, except maybe to make me mad.<br />Nellie's sister, Terel, was the worst character I think I've read about since Amy March. Actually, she could probably give Amy some good competition.<br />And every time it seemed like Nellie was FINALLY going to realize that the only person not lying to her was Jace, she'd fall right back into her old ways until even Jace felt he had to resort to manipulating her.<br /><br />I just can't with this book. If I read this as-is and pretend there's nothing more to it, it would get negative fifteen stars. For my own sanity, I'm going to pretend that it was all a joke and Jude is just having a laugh at all the cliches. I don't know where that leaves me. Three stars implies that I liked this, so I guess it has to be two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15604696867622471617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gQFzCsY1QPlQBZJi8CXZgfv4+tSk0tJ6Qz6oppgt/t9MisLR5fYfyqB45sVq0LypOQo4No4PEhJ0n1foqzXVOA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gShHAVpHj751ostzEmHY/5R70awx1mTdrujlcPuJlIxMo/baeYTQjYXfv9SIlL3XVokTThsLpLWZSRo+yJG/aw==')})
  }

Until small-town life reveals a big problem: she can’t grow unless she learns to let go. If Sophie relaxes her grip even a little, she might lose everything. Or she might finally be free to reach for the happiness and love that have eluded her for so long.\n\nKristine has become defined by her relationship to others. She’s a wife, a mom. As much as she adores her husband and sons, she wants something for herself—a sweet little bakery just off the waterfront. She knew changing the rules wouldn’t be easy, but she never imagined she might have to choose between her marriage and her dreams.\n\nLike the mainland on the horizon, Heather’s goals seem beyond her grasp. Every time she manages to save for college, her mother has another crisis. Can she break free, or will she be trapped in this tiny life forever?\n\nTold with Mallery’s trademark humor and charm, Sisters by Choice is a heartfelt tale of love, family and the friendships that       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/28574.Jude_Deveraux">About Jude Deveraux</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8765700363285218123">Jude Gilliam was born September 20, 1947 in Fairdale, Kentucky. She has a large extended family and is the elder sister of four brothers. She attended Murray State University and received a degree in Art. In 1967, Jude married and took her husband's surname of White, but four years later they divorced. For years, she worked as 5th-grade teacher.<br/><br/>She began writing in 1976, and published her first bo</span>
  <span id="freeText8765700363285218123" style="display:none">Jude Gilliam was born September 20, 1947 in Fairdale, Kentucky. She has a large extended family and is the elder sister of four brothers. She attended Murray State University and received a degree in Art. In 1967, Jude married and took her husband's surname of White, but four years later they divorced. For years, she worked as 5th-grade teacher.<br /><br />She began writing in 1976, and published her first book, <i>The Enchanted Land</i> (1977) under the name Jude Deveraux. Following the publication of her first novel, she resigned her teaching position. Now, she is the author of 31 <i>New York Times</i> bestsellers. <br /><br />Jude won readers' hearts with the epic Velvet series, which revolves around the lives of the Montgomery family's irresistible men. Jude's early books are set largely in 15th- and 16th-century England; in them her fierce, impassioned protagonists find themselves in the midst of blood feuds and wars. Her heroines are equally scrappy -- medieval Scarlett O'Haras who often have a low regard for the men who eventually win them over. They're fighters, certainly, but they're also beauties who are preoccupied with survival and family preservation. <br /><br />Jude has also stepped outside her milieu, with mixed results. Her James River trilogy (<i>River Lady, Lost Lady,</i> and <i>Counterfeit Lady</i>) is set mostly in post-Revolution America; the popular, softer-edged <i>Twin of Fire</i>/<i>Twin of Ice</i> moves to 19th-century Colorado and introduces another hunky-man clan, the Taggerts.<br /><br />Deveraux manages to evoke a strong and convincing atmosphere for each of her books, but her dialogue and characters are as familiar as a modern-day soap opera's. "Historicals seem to be all I'm capable of," Jude once said in an interview, referring to a now out-of-print attempt at contemporary fiction, 1982's <i>Casa Grande</i>. "I don't want to write family sagas or occult books, and I have no intention of again trying to ruin the contemporary market." Still, Jude did later attempt modern-day romances, such as the lighthearted <i>High Tide</i> (her first murder caper), the contemporary female friendship story <i>The Summerhouse</i>, and the time-traveling <i>Knight in Shining Armor</i>. In fact, with 2002's <i>The Mulberry Tree</i>, Deveraux seems to be getting more comfortable setting stories in the present, which is a good thing, since the fans she won with her historical books are eager to follow her into the future.<br /><br />Jude married Claude White, who she later divorced in 1993. Around the same time she met Mohammed Montassir with whom she had a son, Sam Alexander Montassir, in 1997. On Oct. 6th, 2005, Sam died at the age of eight in a motorcycle accident. <br /><br />Jude has lived in several countries and all over the United States. She currently lives in Charlotte, North Carolina and has an additional home in the medieval city of Badolato, Italy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8765700363285218123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
